## ACKNOWLEDGMENTS

Abov all, I am grateful to Max Palevsky for his exceptional generosity in supporting this eibition and LAcMA's collection—his gifts are the principal reason why this museum has one o the world's great repositories of material from the Arts and Crafts movement. He has been not only the major source of philanthropy for the decorative arts department, but also a personal inspiration. He is ne of the rare breed f collectors whose passions are equally divided between aesthetics and ideas, and he is committed to sharing both with the widest possible audience.

I deeply appreciate the support of the senior management at LACMA. First thanks must go to President and Wallis Annenberg Director Andrea Rich, who issued the mandate for this exhibition on my first day at LAcMA and who has always encouraged the highest ambitions for it. Deputy Director of Art Administration and Collections Nancy Thomas has been a wonderful i:cHerel han Dep D of Art Programs Bruce Robertson, whose combination of optimism and sage advice always made the most difficult challenges surmountable.

An exhibition is the ultimate collaborative effort and LACMA is fortunate to have a decorative arts department peopled with gifted, committed museum professionals. Emily Zaiden has devoted herself for the past eighteen months to exhibition organization and interpretation: her keen eye, passion for the subject, and outstanding management skills have contributed emously ts succes. Earlier, Mail Pngel playe an integral rol in shaping the exhibion, especially in the formation of the checklist. Department administrator Christel Guarnieri's determination, patience, design skils, and humor were invaluable contributions to the project.

Thanks are also due to Marcia Rickard and Bobbye Tigerman, who helped with research from turn-of-the-century periodicals; Julia Wheatley skillfully assisted with research as well as locating objects. Stacey Loughrey Sloboda was heroic in ensuring the accuracy of the checklist and other exhibition tasks. Department volunteers Marilyn Gross and Helen De Gyarfas provided much valued assistance. Edith Wachtel kindly provided translation help with what Mark Twain has famously called "the awful German language."

The contributions of the publications department to this book are almost immeasurable, especially those of editor Nola Butler. She has an exemplary ear for language, eye for detail, and feel for how a book should be shaped, and she combined these skills with an extraordinarily perceptive and rapid mastery of the subject matter. Director of Publications Stephanie Emerson provided expert oversight of every aspect of production; Sara Cody greatly helped with the checklist; Erika Caswell assisted with countless details; and freelance proofreader Dianne Woo and indexer Kathleen Preciado applied their excellent skills despite compressed schedules. Cheryle Robertson navigated the shoals of rights and reproductions with tenacity and admirable good humor. We were truly fortunate to have secured the participation of book designer Lorraine Wild, ably assisted by Stuart Smith; their exceptional graphic talents and great sensitivity to the material were matched by their grace under pressure. Peter Brenner and Steve Oliver in the photographic services department were responsible for beautiful new shots of the works at LACMA and in local collections.

Grateful acknowledgment must also be extended to the exhibitions department—Irene Martín, Beverley Sabo, Kristin Fredricks, and Elaine Peterson—who worked tirelessly on the myriad details of the tour and the budget. The daunting logistical and insurance issues involving the safe transportation of objects from thirteen countries were skillfully handled by Renée Montgomery, Ted Greenberg, Portland McCormick, Jennifer Garpner, and Jennifer Yates. Without Del Magpantay's enthusiastic and patient assistance, we could never have kept track of the status of each and every exhibition object.

The conservation department provided exemplary help throughout the years of planning. The exhibition includes as many media as it does countries, and I deeply appreciate the extensive contributions made by Victoria Blyth-Hill, John Hirx, Soko Furuhata, Jennifer Koerner, and Katrina Posner. A special debt is owed to Catherine McLean and Don Menveg, whose superb coordination of all textile and furniture issues went far beyond professional duty. Curators Dale Gluckman and Timothy Benson also exceeded the call of collegiality by generously providing eiinhe eldstextiles angraphicrt repectively.CriVigilet andRobyn Sanr in the Rifkind Center provided great assistance with loans of works on paper.

The education department, especially Jane Burrell and Mary Lenihan, contributed much to the success of special programs and exhibition interpretation. Chris Hansen, Bo Smith, and Kirsten Schmidt did an outstanding job devising a marketing plan and generating publicity. Nancy Sutherland and Angelo Gabriel in the Balch Research Library were extremely helpful with interlibrary loans and research.

Bringing to the project a great sensitivity to the most advantageous display of objects as well as the logistical problems of correct placement, Bernard Kester created a beautiful installation. Amy McFarland and Katherine Go imaginatively demonstrated how graphic design can enhance both the aesthetics and interpretation of an exhibition. Art Owens and Bill Stahl in the operations department made the most of the construction budget, and I am grateful for their creativity and commitment. Jeff Haskin and his team of art installers displayed their customary consummate professionalism to ensure the safety of the objects when placed in the galleries and in preparation for travel.

The interdisciplinary skills required to examine the breadth and complexity of the Arts and Crafts movement were provided by a number of scholars outside LACMA. In addition to writing essays and sharing their exceptional expertise, the exhibition consultants were essential to determining the location and selection of objects. I am profoundly grateful to contributors Alan Crawford, Rüdiger Joppien, Juliet Kinchin, Amy Ogata, Christian Witt-Dörring, and Elisabet Stavenow-Hidemark. Consultants Derek Ostergard and Wendy Salmond also made significant contributions to the shaping of the exhibition.

In addition, many other colleagues demonstrated extraordinary generosity. For the American essay, Director of the Gamble House Edward Bosley not only read more drafts than any friend could expect, but also made astute comments about them. An expert in American pottery and glass, Alice Frelinghuysen of the Metropolitan Museum of Art contributed greatly to the selection of ceramics. Bruce Barnes, Joseph Cunningham, Stephen Gray, and Marilee Meyer shared their superb connoisseurship skills, knowledge of collections, and the most current research about American designers. Barbara McCarthy and Susan Potter in Max Palevsky's office kindly went out of their way to assist with many aspects of the exhibition.

Professor Nicola Gordon Bowe's efforts to help select and confirm the loans from Ireland were nothing short of heroic, and I cannot thank her enough for sharing her incomparable knowledge of the Irish Arts and Crafts movement. My knowledge of the Nordic countries was vastly enhanced by Mirjam Gelfer-Jorgensen in Denmark, Marianne Aav in Finland, Widar Halén in Norway, and Micael Ernstell in Sweden. These scholars were also extraordinarily helpful in securing loans for the exhibition. Zsuzsanna Vámos-Lovay, deputy director at the Museum of Applied Arts, Budapest, was exceptionally generous in helping with all the Hungarian loans. Peter Cormack at the William Morris Gallery, Mary Greensted at the Cheltenham Art Gallery and Museum, and Pamela Robertson at the Hunterian Art Gallery, University of Glasgow, insightfully advised on the selection of British objects.

The challenge of re-creating the dining room that Peter Behrens designed for the Wertheim department store would have been overwhelming without the expert advice and aweinspiring efforts of Laurie Stein at the University of Chicago and Renate Ulmer, chief curator of the Städtische Kunstsammlung in Darmstadt. Laurie's collaboration with Jo Hormuth, the outstanding artist who made the stenciled walls and carpet, combined meticulous scholarship with a rare sensibility about historic colors and methods of fabrication. They also advised on the re-creation of the Behrens light fixture, which was the ambitious undertaking of Dr. Hofu Wu of Cal Poly Pomona, together with his talented students Omrana Ahmed, Jeremy Fong, Rodolfo Gonzalez, and Francis Ly. Additional research was generously provided by Volker Doehne and Sabine Roeder at the Krefelder Kunstmuseen; Albrecht Pyritz; Hans Ottomeyer at the Deutsches Historisches Museum; and the company Kunsch Metallbau, Berlin.

The following individuals and colleagues at other institutions are among the many who were generous with their collections and expertise: Paul Asenbaum and Isabella Croy at Asenbaum Fine Arts; Candace Key at the Backhausen company; Nina Stritzler-Levine at the Bard Graduate Center; Ingeborg Becker at the Bröhan-Museum; Ann Chaves and André Chaves; Fr. Cathal Geraghty at the Clonfert Diocesan Museum; Simon Olding and Jean Vacher at the Crafts Study Centre at the Surrey Institute of Art and Design; Elizabeth Cumming; Bodil Busk Laursen and Charlotte Malte Kelly at the Danish Museum of Design and Art, Copenhagen; Lieven Daenens at the Design Museum, Gent; Peyton Skipwith and Annamarie Stapleton at the Fine Art Society; David Britton at the Frederick Gallery; Robert Furhoff; Anne Mallek at the Gamble House; Peter Trowles at the Glasgow School of Art; Mária Merva Gaál at the Gödolló Municipal Museum; Martin Levy at H. Blairman and Sons; Helen Dunstan and Michael Whiteway at Haslam and Whiteway; Thomas Heinz; Wolfgang Glüber at the Hessisches Landesmuseum Darmstadt; Laszlo Kiss Horvath; Margarita Cappock at the Hugh Lane; Tibor Kovacs and Lilla Tompos at the Hungarian National Museum; Alan Jutzi, Shelley Bennett, Diane Waggoner, Jessica Todd Smith, and John Murdoch at the Huntington Library, Art Collections, and Botanical Gardens; Dr. and Mrs. Hermann Kleinstück; Ellen and Harvey Knell; Catherine Kurland; Harold Nelson at the Long Beach Museum of Art; Randell Makinson; Katalin Gellér at the Magyar Tudományos Akadémia; Nancy McLelland; Suzanne Flynt at the Memorial Hall Museum; Jane Adlin, J. Stewart Johnson, and Amelia Peck at the Metropolitan Museum of Art; Helmut Bauer at the Münchner Stadtmuseum Die Möbelsammlung; Agnès Delannoy at the Musée Départmental Maurice Denis; Peter Stohler and Eva Afuhs at the Museum Bellerive, Zurich; Elisabeth Schmuttermeier and Angela Völker at the Museum fur Angewandte Kunst; Éva Csenkey, Vera Varga, and Simon Károly at the Museum of Applied Arts, Budapest; Timo Keinänen at the Museum of Finnish Architecture; Pál Ritoók at the Museum of Hugarian Architecture; Anniken Thue at the Nasjonalgalleriet, Oslo; D. Dodge Thompson at the National Gallery of Art, Washington; Hilary Pyle at the National Gallery of Ireland; Ritva Wäre at the National Museum of Finland; Raghnall ó Floinn, and Patrick Wallace at the National Museum of Ireland; Gyorgy Balázs at the Néprajzi Múzeum, Budapest; Jan-Lauritz Opstad at the Nordenfjeldske Kunstindustrimuseum, Trondheim; Ernst Ploil; Marketta Tamminen at the Porvoo Museum; Paul Reeves; Charles Hind at RIBA; Elsebeth Welander-Berggren at the Röhsska Museet; Tibor Fényi at the Róth Miksa Museum, Budapest; Siobhán Fitzpatrick at the Royal Irish Academy; Werner Adriaenssens, Sara De Coninck, and Clare Dumortier at the Royal Museums of Art and History, Brussels; Cara McCarty and Pam Stewart at the Saint Louis Art Museum; Udo Schröder; Christopher Jordan at the South London Gallery; Klaus Wolbert at the Städtische Kunstsammlung Darmstadt; David and Sonya Newell-mi heTae Galley; EeonDoaldTafe; Dul Tuce; GrahaDry at Von Zezschwitz Kunst urid Design; Cathy Leff and Marianne Lamonaca at the Wolfsonian—FIU; David Woodruff; and Lori Zabar.

The contributions of my sister and brother-in-law, Debbie and Mark Attanasio, must be specially noted. Not only did they generously underwrite the Arts and Crafts movement symposium at LACMA and lend a key object to the exhibition, but they have also added immeasurably to my life in Los Angeles. Debbie has been steadfast in continuing atradition begun in grade shool of editing my work and taking care of me.

Last, Iwould like thank my friends in Los Angeles epecially Katharine DeShaw, Marcella Rubleand Nancy Troy, who proviethepor ncrgemen sentil he cpl of this work.

WENDY KAPLAN

Department Head and Curator

![](images/e9ec69a3b664dd73aed287977a06ed7d712e9b72dcbe7578ce0e046595ca0cdc.jpg)

![](images/6f0ce00539a5358cf58a696e3ef16773ecb097381d5c4643b3c7d2f3f0d6e3f9.jpg)

Wendy Kaplan, department head and curator of decorative arts at the Los Angeles County Museum of Art, has written or co-authored many books about the history of design, including Designing Modernity: The Arts of Reform and Persuasion, 1885—1945, The Arts and Crafts Movement and 'The Art that is Life': The Arts and Crafts Movement in America.

Alan Crawford, a leading authority on the British Arts and Crafts movement, has written C.R.Ashbee: Architect, Designer, and Romantic Socialist and Charles Rennie Mackintosh; he also coauthored By Hammer and Hand: The Arts and Crafts Movement in Birmingham.

Rüdiger Joppien is senior curator of decorative arts at the Museum für Kunst und Gewerbe, Hamburg, and head of the department of Art Nouveau and modernism. He is the author of many publications on twentieth-century decorative arts, including Europäischer Jugendstil, Louis C. Tiffany and Hermann und Richard Mutz — Keramik des Jugendstils.

Juliet Kinchin, a senior lecturer at Glasgow University, is the author of The Glasgow Style and Glasgow's Great Exhibitions.

Amy F. Ogata, associate professor at the Bard Graduate Center for Studies in the Decorative Arts, Design and Culture, has published the book Art Nouveau and the Social Vision of Modern Living: Belgian Artists in a European Context.

Elisabet Stavenow-Hidemark, Ph.D, is a curator emeritus at the Nordiska Museet in Stockholm. She co-authored Carl and Karin Larsson: Creators of the Swedish Style, as well as many other books on Swedish applied arts.

Christian Witt-Dörring, curator of furniture and woodwork at the Museum für Angewandte Kunst (MAK - Austrian Museum of Applied Arts), Vienna, has contributed to many publications, including Josef Hoffmann Designs and Der Preis der Schönheit: 100 Jahre Wiener Werkstätte.

THAMES & HUDSON, INC.

500 FIFTH AVENUE
